      <text xml:space="preserve">{{Refimprove|date=November 2014}}
[[File:Poi circles.jpg|thumb|right|A flower pattern from flow artist Nick Woolsey captured through long exposure photography; photograph is an example of [[light painting]]]]
'''Glowsticking''' is a form of [[object manipulation]] or [[dancing]] with [[glowstick]]s or other glowstick-like objects that share the same qualities: durability, consistency in light, safe to toss around, and the material of which they are made, often a soft and pliant [[plastic]].
''Glowsticking'' is an &quot;umbrella term&quot; describing two broad categories, with the most agreed upon separation being whether it is stringed or not stringed. More importantly, glowsticking has roots in the [[electronica]] and [[rave]] scenes, and has a cultural paradigm more in common with those scenes than those of other scenes. Some aspects include the culture of non-competitiveness, preferring sharing and performing in accordance with your observer, without any kind of negative statement implied. Because of this glowsticking competitions are frowned upon by most practitioners of glowsticking. Although glowsticking as a field can largely be practiced anywhere, the roots it has with raving has led to the adoption of most of the ideals of the rave scene. In recent days complete glow stick costumes have been created that attach to one's body, the two most popular being from Crayola and Glowstickables.&lt;ref&gt;[http://www.glowsticking.com/articles-and-tutorials/culture/71-glowsticking-culture/113-what-is-glowsticking.html What is Glowsticking?], ''Glowsticking.com Articles,'' 2002&lt;/ref&gt;
==Forms==
Both of these terms, freehand and glowstringing, describe the technical skills that relates to both. It is only when the practitioner intends to [[dance]] that it becomes glowsticking. Otherwise, they may be a [[juggler]] who is simply choosing to juggle glowsticks (in the case of freehand), or a poist who is doing [[poi (performance art)|poi]] with glowsticks. That is not to say that a juggler or a poist cannot dance if they so choose with glowsticks—just that glowsticking implies dancing.&lt;ref&gt;[http://www.glowsticking.com/articles-and-tutorials/culture/71-glowsticking-culture/113-what-is-glowsticking.html Forms of Glowsticking.], ''Glowsticking.com Articles,'' 2002&lt;/ref&gt;
===Glowstringing===
Glowstringing is defined by a few factors: the use of glowsticks on a string, the swinging motion, and an equally large growing category of moves and concepts that share many of the same aspects as many other stringing related fields, such as [[poi (performance art)|poi]], [[yo-yo]]ing, and [[martial arts]] forms common with [[sword]]s, [[flail]]s, and [[rope dart]]s, is typically done with glowstick or glowstick-like instruments tied with a durable string at the end of it. In some case, handles may be used, because of moves which favor the fact that the glowstick handle can be grabbed and switched with the swinging part. In some cases, because of the existence of handles which glow both ways, moves which &quot;throw&quot; can be accomplished as it can be grabbed on either side.&lt;ref&gt;[http://www.glowsticking.com/articles-and-tutorials/culture/71-glowsticking-culture/113-what-is-glowsticking.html What is Glowstringing?], ''Glowsticking.com Articles,'' 2002&lt;/ref&gt;
===Freehand===
Freehand glowsticking is glowsticking typically practiced without strings attached to the glowsticks.  Freehand is defined by the steadily growing body of concepts and moves. Some of these concepts include tracing, taps, tossing, stalls and threading, as well as interdisciplinary dance skills borrowed from common [[funk style]] categories. Freehand glowsticking typically borrows from many other dance styles such as [[liquid dancing]] as well as having its own unique set of moves.&lt;ref&gt;[http://www.glowsticking.com/articles-and-tutorials/culture/71-glowsticking-culture/113-what-is-glowsticking.html What is Freehand?], ''Glowsticking.com Articles,'' 2002&lt;/ref&gt;
Tracing is the act of dragging the glowsticks over the contours of one's body. An example of a common trace is the stomach trace, which includes dragging the glow sticks over one's stomach to create a circular pattern.  Another example of a basic movement frequently used in freehand glowsticking is the figure eight—quite possibly the most well known, albeit not the most common move in the intermediate and more advanced levels.
===Lightshows===
In the context of this article, a lightshow is a [[performance]] given with glowsticks to a small audience of one or several people which are physically close to the [[performer]]. Lightshow is a term that can be used loosely to refer to performances given with LED lights ([[light-emitting diodes]]), assorted [[light]] [[toy]]s, [[lasers]], and a variety of other &quot;light up&quot; items.&lt;ref&gt;[http://www.glowsticking.com/articles-and-tutorials/culture/71-glowsticking-culture/141-the-lightshow.html The Lightshow.], ''Glowsticking.com Articles,'' 02-13-2008&lt;/ref&gt;
==History and culture==
Although glowsticking has roots in the mid-1980s gay scene in the US at [[Saint (nightclub)|Saint nightclub]] in New York and in the UK at [[Heaven (nightclub)|Heaven nightclub]] before becoming popular in the early 1990s on the underground [[rave]] scene, they were used in Grateful Dead shows before the rave scene arrived, it has since become a separate cultural phenomenon that can be found throughout the general [[electronic dance music]] world, and is becoming popular in the [[twirling]] and [[:Category:Physical activity and dexterity toys|dexterity play]] communities.&lt;ref&gt;{{cite book |author=Torgovnick K|title=Cheer!: Inside the Secret World of College Cheerleaders |publisher= [[Simon &amp; Schuster|Touchstone]] |location=New York, NY |year=2009 |pages= 117 |isbn=1-4165-3597-7 |oclc= |doi= |accessdate=}}&lt;/ref&gt;
There has been some who have claimed glowstringing is [[poi (performance art)|poi]] with [[glowstick]]s. This confusion is understandable, as the field of glowstringing is smaller and newer than the field of poi. Poi as a cultural art form is a hundreds of years old discipline coming from [[New Zealand]].
Glowstringing originally came from Poists who practiced the art at [[rave]]s, where glowsticks were probably advantageous compared to non-glowing objects. Many glowstringers can probably trace their roots to poi and many will often practice more poi at times than &quot;pure&quot; glowstringing.
Glowsticks were preferred by many in the rave scene in a way much similar to freehand's development, and were preferred in the rave scene to emit light for a numerous reasons, including its relative cheapness, their harmlessness and durability and their disposable nature, but has largely cemented glowsticks as an icon of the rave scene, sometimes negatively, which is why there was and is still such a large prevalence of glowstick use by freehanders and glowstringers alike.
The nature of the glowstick, allowing for concepts which would otherwise be impossible with other objects, has thus significantly influenced the development of both freehand and glowstringing. In freehand, the obvious shape of the glowstick is used in numerous ways to accent, or to catch, or to even create patterns of light or to accentuate body movement. In terms of glowstringing, glowsticks have significantly impacted former pure poists in order to take advantage of the glowstick. For example, linked catches and glowstick manipulations borrow far more from a [[yo-yo]] string manipulation concept than poi.
Over time, glowstringing, because of the cultural differences that resulted from many different reasons, has become its own category. In all, glowstringing belongs in the same category of swinging objects and object manipulation such as [[Poi (performance art)|Poi]], martial arts, [[yo-yo]]ing, [[Fire staff|staffing]], etc.&lt;ref&gt;[http://www.glowsticking.com/articles-and-tutorials/culture/71-glowsticking-culture/113-what-is-glowsticking.html An Explanation Of The History Of Freehand And Glowstringing.], ''Glowsticking.com Articles,'' 2002&lt;/ref&gt;
==Criticism==
The origin of &quot;ravers&quot; using glowsticks started when they used them to &quot;blow each other up&quot; by twirling glowsticks and LED lights in front of one another's face.{{citation needed|date=September 2013}} This is thought to enhance the effects of the drug MDMA, or ecstasy, which is a popular drug among ravers and the rave scene. Some rave promoters have banned glowsticks from events, especially those taking place in confined spaces, due to the space required to glow stick and the potential danger of striking other rave goers.{{Citation needed|date=November 2008}} In 2001, the [[Drug Enforcement Administration|DEA]] tried but failed to ban glowsticks and other items from dance parties, mislabeling them &quot;drug paraphernalia.&quot; &lt;ref&gt;[https://www.aclu.org/news/governments-war-raves-went-too-far-louisiana-court-rules Government's War on Raves Went Too Far, Louisiana Court Rules (8/24/2001)]&lt;/ref&gt;

'''Legislative elections''' were held on 23 September 2001.
==Results==
{{Politics of Macau}}
The results, as published in the 41st SAR Gazette following verification by the Court of Final Appeal, were:
* 83,644 voters (52.34% of the registered voters) had cast votes
* 80,978 votes were valid
* 2,116 were invalid
* 550 were blank
*1. [[Antonio Ng|Antonio Ng Kuok Cheong]] (ANMD, with 16, 961 votes)
*2. Kwan Tsui Hang (UPD, with 12, 990 votes) 
*3. Leong Heng Teng (UPP, 11 276 votes) 
*4. Chow Kam Fai, David (CODEM, with 10, 016 votes) 
*5. Vitor Cheung Lup Kwan ( ARSEM, with 9, 955 votes) 
*6. Au Kam San (ANMD, with 8, 480.5 votes) 
*7. Leong Iok Wa ( UPD, with 6, 495 votes) 
*8. Iong Weng Ian (UPP, with 5, 638 votes) 
*9. João Bosco Cheang (AEA, with 5, 170 votes) 
*10. Jorge Manuel Fão (CODEM, with 5, 008 votes)
Members for indirect returned of the Legislative Assembly in the second term:
*Chan Chak Mo and Fong Chi Keong (DCAR –Group representing welfare, cultural, educational and sports interests: with 1 364 votes) 
*Susana Chou, Hoi Sai Iun, Kou Hoi In and Cheang Chi Keong (OMKC Group representing business: with 279 votes) 
*Lao Cheok Va and Tong Chi Kin (CCCAE Group representing labor: with 261 votes) 
*Chui Sai Cheong and Leonel Alberto Alves (OMCY Group representing professional: with 188 votes)

'''''The Best of the Monkees''''' is a [[The Monkees|Monkees]] compilation released by [[Rhino Entertainment]]. It contains 25 songs from The Monkees' repertoire, listed in chronological order by release date. Also included is a Bonus [[karaoke]] CD with five tracks. Unlike previous Rhino compilations, this one does not include any material from the 1980s or 1990s reunions, focusing strictly on the band's 1960s output.
''The Best of the Monkees'' replaced ''[[Greatest Hits (1995 The Monkees album)|The Monkees Greatest Hits]]'', released in 1995 in anticipation of the band’s 30th Anniversary celebration the following year.
The album debuted on the [[Billboard 200|''Billboard'' 200]] in the issue dated May 17, 2003, at number 51. It spent six weeks on the chart. Following the death of member [[Davy Jones (actor)|Davy Jones]] on February 29, 2012, it re-entered at No. 20 with 17,000 copies sold (up 7,808 percent according to [[Nielsen SoundScan]]) for the week ending March 4, 2012. The album has since been certified Gold for selling 500,000 copies.

'''David Anthony Lucas''' (born 23 November 1977) is an English professional [[association football|footballer]] who plays for [[Fleetwood Town F.C.|Fleetwood Town]].
Lucas currently acts as the goalkeeper coach at Fleetwood, as well as retaining his registration as the club's senior goalkeeper. He has made 307 appearances in [[the Football League]], including 118 for [[Preston North End F.C.|Preston North End]].
Lucas began his career at his hometown club Preston North End in the [[Football League Third Division]]. He spent time on loan at [[Darlington F.C.|Darlington]], [[Scunthorpe United F.C.|Scunthorpe United]], and [[Sheffield Wednesday F.C.|Sheffield Wednesday]], before signing for Sheffield Wednesday in 2004. He then joined rivals [[Barnsley F.C.|Barnsley]] in 2007, but only made three appearances for them before signing with [[Leeds United F.C.|Leeds United]] in the same year. After spending much of the [[2007-08 in English football|2007–08 season]] as an unused substitute, he began to establish himself as the first choice goalkeeper at Elland Road, impressing manager [[Gary McAllister]] with a series of good displays continuing into the following season. He made a number of appearances before being dropped in December, subsequently only appearing on the bench. He signed for [[Swindon Town F.C.|Swindon Town]] in June 2009. Lucas had a successful season in which he played a major part in Swindon reaching the [[Football League One play-offs]]. Lucas' contract with Swindon was terminated one year early by mutual consent, and he signed a one-year deal with [[Rochdale A.F.C.|Rochdale]] on 3 August 2011, taking up a player/coach role. Lucas was released by Rochdale at the end of the season, before he signed a one-year contract with [[Football League Championship|Championship]] club [[Birmingham City F.C.|Birmingham City]] on 10 July 2012. He made one appearance before leaving when the January 2013 transfer window opened, to join League Two club Fleetwood Town, reuniting with former Preston North End teammates [[Graham Alexander]], now manager of Fleetwood, and first team coach [[Chris Lucketti]].
Lucas has played internationally for England, five times at under-18 and four times at under-20 level.
== Club career ==
=== Preston North End ===
As a young [[Goalkeeper (association football)|goalkeeper]], Lucas started his career at [[Preston North End F.C.|Preston North End]]. He went on to spend nearly ten years as a professional at the [[Lancashire]] club, punctuated by loan appearances for [[Darlington F.C.|Darlington]], [[Scunthorpe United F.C.|Scunthorpe]] and [[Sheffield Wednesday]]. Lucas was capped by [[England national under-18 football team|England under-18]] and [[England national under-20 football team|under-20]] teams while a Preston player.&lt;!--
there are no contemporary sources for him winning u21 caps: his profile at the FA gives U18 and U20 only, and he isn't in the list of U21 internationals in the Sky Sports annual
--&gt;&lt;ref&gt;{{cite web |url=http://www.thefa.com/England/All-Teams/Players?p=314259 |title=David Lucas |publisher=The Football Association |accessdate=19 August 2012}}&lt;/ref&gt;
=== Sheffield Wednesday ===
Lucas had another spell at Sheffield Wednesday, having signed a permanent deal with the [[Yorkshire]] side in the summer of 2004 after impressing during his two loan spells the previous season. During Wednesday's promotion [[2004–05 in English football|season of 2004–05]], Lucas made 41 appearances for the team and totalled 15 [[clean sheet]]s, despite twice having to battle against injuries.
Lucas started the first 18 matches of Sheffield Wednesday's [[2005–06 in English football|2005–06]] campaign before a knee injury again ruled him out until January. His comeback was short-lived and Lucas was injured again against [[Millwall F.C.|Millwall]] on 4 February 2006 after playing only two full games; the new injury again ruled him out until January 2007.
Lucas announced that he would not be renewing his contract with Sheffield Wednesday at the end of the 2005–06 season, although he continued to receive treatment at their training ground whilst he was recovering from his knee injury.&lt;ref&gt;{{cite news |url=http://news.bbc.co.uk/sport1/hi/football/teams/s/sheff_wed/5094912.stm |title=Keeper Lucas to quit Hillsborough |date=19 June 2006 |publisher=BBC Sport |accessdate=1 August 2009}}&lt;/ref&gt;
=== Barnsley ===
Lucas subsequently joined [[South Yorkshire]] rivals [[Barnsley F.C.|Barnsley]] on a free transfer in January 2007,&lt;ref&gt;{{cite news |url=http://news.bbc.co.uk/sport1/hi/football/teams/b/barnsley/6228877.stm |title=Barnsley snap up Lucas and McCann |date=3 January 2007 |publisher=BBC Sport |accessdate=1 August 2009}}&lt;/ref&gt; but only made three appearances for them. During his first game for Barnsley, he came out to deal with a high ball and collided with the [[Derby County F.C.|Derby County]] player [[Giles Barnes]]. He was knocked unconscious and left the field on a [[spinal board]] after several minutes' treatment. He was expected to need at least ten days to recover from [[concussion]].&lt;ref&gt;{{cite news |url=http://www.sportinglife.com/football/news/article/165/7934158/barnsley-1-derby-2 |title=Barnsley 1 Derby 2 |first=Ben |last=Rumsby |agency=PA Sport |work=sportinglife.com |publisher=365 Media Group |date=31 March 2007 |accessdate=19 August 2012}}&lt;/ref&gt;&lt;ref&gt;{{cite news |url=http://www.thesun.co.uk/sol/homepage/sport/football/23767/Barnsley-1-Derby-2.html |title=Barnsley 1 Derby 2 |first=Martin |last=Blackburn |work=The Sun |date=1 April 2007 |accessdate=19 August 2012}}&lt;/ref&gt;
=== Leeds United ===
Lucas signed for [[Leeds United F.C.|Leeds United]] in September 2007 on a short term contract,&lt;ref&gt;{{cite news |url=http://news.bbc.co.uk/sport1/hi/football/teams/l/leeds_united/6989669.stm |title=Goalkeeper Lucas earns Leeds deal |date=11 September 2007 |publisher=BBC Sport |accessdate=1 August 2009}}&lt;/ref&gt; making his debut in the [[Football League Trophy]] second round against [[Darlington F.C.|Darlington]].
He was released in May 2009.&lt;ref&gt;{{cite news |url=http://news.bbc.co.uk/sport1/hi/football/teams/l/leeds_united/8063666.stm |title=Douglas and Lucas to leave Leeds |date=22 May 2009 |publisher=BBC Sport |accessdate=1 August 2009}}&lt;/ref&gt;
=== Swindon Town ===
Lucas signed for [[Swindon Town F.C.|Swindon Town]] in June 2009 on a two-year contract.&lt;ref&gt;{{cite news |url=http://news.bbc.co.uk/sport1/hi/football/teams/s/swindon_town/8076547.stm |title=Swindon bring in goalkeeper Lucas |date=2 June 2009 |publisher=BBC Sport |accessdate=10 July 2009}}&lt;/ref&gt; He was assigned the number 1 jersey with previous incumbent [[Phil Smith (footballer born 1979)|Phil Smith]] being relegated to the number 12.&lt;ref&gt;{{cite web |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20091002094857/http://www.swindontownfc.co.uk/page/NewsDetail/0,,10341~1734252,00.html |title=Updated squad list |date=5 August 2009 |publisher=Swindon Town F.C |archivedate=2 October 2009|url=http://www.swindontownfc.co.uk/page/NewsDetail/0,,10341~1734252,00.html }}&lt;/ref&gt; Lucas had a successful season, which played a major part in Swindon reaching the [[Football League One play-offs]]. He played in both legs of the semi-final against [[Charlton Athletic F.C.|Charlton Athletic]], but injured his shoulder in the second minute of the second leg and played no further part in the competition.
=== Rochdale ===
Lucas' contract with Swindon was terminated one year early by mutual consent, and he signed a one-year deal with [[Rochdale A.F.C.|Rochdale]] on 3 August 2011, taking up a player/coach role.&lt;ref&gt;{{cite news|url=http://www.rochdaleafc.co.uk/page/NewsDetail/0,,10441~2409417,00.html#continue |title=Lucas Joins Ranks |publisher=Rochdale A.F.C |date=3 August 2011 |accessdate=10 August 2011 |deadurl=yes |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20120323075410/http://www.rochdaleafc.co.uk/page/NewsDetail/0,,10441~2409417,00.html |archivedate=23 March 2012 |df=dmy }}&lt;/ref&gt; He made his Rochdale playing debut in the League Cup against [[Chesterfield F.C.|Chesterfield]] on 9 August. Lucas was released by Rochdale at the end of the season.
=== Birmingham City and Fleetwood Town ===
Lucas signed a one-year contract with [[Football League Championship|Championship]] club [[Birmingham City F.C.|Birmingham City]] on 10 July 2012.&lt;ref&gt;{{cite news |url=http://www.bbc.co.uk/sport/0/football/18784511 |title=David Lucas becomes Birmingham City's latest signing |date=10 July 2012 |publisher=BBC Sport |accessdate=19 August 2012}}&lt;/ref&gt; He made his debut on 14 August in the first round of the League Cup at home to [[Barnet F.C.|Barnet]].&lt;ref&gt;{{cite news |url=http://www1.skysports.com/football/live/match/265705/report |title=Blues hammer sorry Bees in cup |date=14 August 2012 |publisher=BBC Sport |accessdate=19 August 2012}}&lt;/ref&gt; That was the only appearance he made before leaving when the January 2013 transfer window opened. He joined League Two club [[Fleetwood Town F.C.|Fleetwood Town]], reuniting with former Preston North End teammates [[Graham Alexander]], now manager of Fleetwood, and first team coach [[Chris Lucketti]]. He joined as goalkeeping coach while retaining his playing registration.&lt;ref&gt;{{cite web |url=http://www.bcfc.com/news/article/lucas-joins-fleetwood-572043.aspx |title=Lucas joins Fleetwood |date=1 January 2013 |publisher=Birmingham City F.C |accessdate=1 January 2013}}&lt;/ref&gt; He made his league début for Fleetwood on 16 February 2013 against [[Burton Albion F.C.|Burton Albion]] coming on as a substitute in the 57th minute after regular goalkeeper [[Scott Davies (footballer born 1987)|Scott Davies]] was sent off. Lucas let in four goals and the game ended in a 4–0 defeat.&lt;ref&gt;{{cite news|url=http://www.bbc.co.uk/sport/0/football/21448255|title=Fleetwood 0–4 Burton|publisher=BBC Sport|date=16 February 2013|accessdate=1 November 2014}}&lt;/ref&gt;
== Honours ==
'''Sheffield Wednesday'''

&lt;!-- bottom --&gt;
| title = [[Chancellor of Germany|Chancellor]]/Chairman [[Council of the People's Deputies]]
| posttitle = Resulting head of government
| before_election = [[Friedrich Ebert]]
| before_party = Social Democratic Party of Germany
| after_election = [[Philipp Scheidemann]], ''Ministerpräsident''
| after_party = Social Democratic Party of Germany
}}
'''Federal elections''' were held in Germany on 19 January 1919,&lt;ref name=NS&gt;[[Dieter Nohlen|Nohlen, D]] &amp; Stöver, P (2010) ''Elections in Europe: A data handbook'', p762 ISBN 978-3-8329-5609-7&lt;/ref&gt; although members of the standing army in the east voted for their representatives only on 2 February. The elections were the first of the new [[Weimar Republic]] following [[World War I]] and the [[German Revolution of 1918–19|Revolution of 1918–19]]. It was also the first German election held using [[proportional representation]] and with [[women's suffrage]]. It is also reckoned as the first truly free and fair all-German election, as it was the first to be held after the scrapping of the old constituencies that grossly over-represented rural areas. The [[voting age]] was lowered to 20 from 25 in the last [[German federal election, 1912|Reichstag election of 1912]].
[[Austrian citizenship|Austrian citizens]] living in Germany were allowed to vote, in the same way that [[German citizenship|German citizens]] living in Austria were also allowed to vote in the [[Austrian Constitutional Assembly election, 1919|Austrian Constitutional Assembly election]] in the same year.&lt;ref&gt;[https://query.nytimes.com/mem/archive-free/pdf?res=F30F1FFD3A5D147A93C4A81789D85F4D8185F9 Austria votes today. –  German Part of Former Dual Monarchy Chooses Its Constituent Assembly.], ''[[The New York Times]]'', 16 February 1919 ([[Portable Document Format|PDF]])&lt;/ref&gt;
From its inaugural session on 6 February, the [[Weimar National Assembly|National Assembly]] (''Nationalversammlung'') functioned as both a [[constituent assembly]] and [[unicameral legislature]]. On 13 February, provisional ''Reichspräsident'' (President) [[Friedrich Ebert]] appointed [[Philipp Scheidemann]] ''Reichsministerpräsident'' (Minister President, the office was renamed [[Chancellor of Germany|Chancellor]] only when the [[Weimar Constitution]] came into force in August 1919). [[Cabinet Scheidemann|Scheidemann's government]] replaced the revolutionary ''Rat der Volksbeauftragten'' ([[Council of the People's Deputies]]). The supporting parties of the &quot;[[Weimar Coalition]]&quot; ([[Social Democratic Party of Germany|SPD]], [[Centre Party (Germany)|Zentrum]] and [[German Democratic Party|DDP]]) together won 76.2% of the votes cast. Voter turnout was 83.0%.&lt;ref&gt;Nohlen &amp; Stöver, p776&lt;/ref&gt;

      <text xml:space="preserve">{{hatnote|For other persons named John Wilson, see [[John Wilson (disambiguation)]].}}
{{unreferenced|date=April 2009}}
[[Image:John Henry Wilson.jpg|thumb|John Henry Wilson]]
'''John Henry Wilson''' (14 February 1834 &amp;ndash; 3 July 1912) was a [[Canadian]] [[physician]], [[professor]], and [[Member of Parliament|parliamentarian]].  A [[Liberal Party of Canada|Liberal]], he served two terms as a [[Member of Parliament]] representing the [[electoral district (Canada)|electoral district]] of [[Elgin East]] in the [[provinces and territories of Canada|province]] of [[Ontario]]. He also represented Elgin East in the [[Legislative Assembly of Ontario]] from 1871 to 1879.
He was born near [[Ottawa]] in 1834, the grandson of a [[United Empire Loyalist]]. He studied medicine at the Toronto School of Medicine (later the Faculty of Medicine at the [[University of Toronto]]) and  [[New York University]]. He received his [[Doctor of Medicine|M.D.]] in 1859 and was appointed professor of [[anatomy]] at [[Victoria University in the University of Toronto|Victoria College]]. In 1860, he opened a medical practice in [[St. Thomas, Ontario]]. He was elected to the provincial legislature in 1871 and 1875. He was elected to the federal parliament in the [[Canadian federal election, 1882|Canadian federal election of 1882]] and was re-elected in [[Canadian federal election, 1887|1887]]. On 8 March 1904 he was appointed to the [[Canadian Senate]] upon the recommendation of Sir [[Wilfrid Laurier]]. He represented the senatorial division of St. Thomas, Ontario until his death in 1912.

'''Craig Doyle''' (born 17 December 1970 in [[Dublin]], [[Republic of Ireland|Ireland]]) is an [[Irish people|Irish]] television and radio presenter. To British viewers he is recognisable as working for the [[BBC]] and [[ITV Network|ITV]]. To Irish viewers he is recognisable as working for [[Raidió Teilifís Éireann]] (RTÉ), and as the host of [[RTÉ One]] chat show ''[[Tonight with Craig Doyle]]'' and [[RTÉ Two]]'s ''[[The Social (Irish TV series)|The Social]]'', now titled ''[[Craig Doyle Live]]'' and broadcast twice a week. He is a regular presenter on [[BT Sport]] rugby coverage.
==Early life==
Doyle grew up in the south Dublin suburb of [[Stillorgan]]. While he was being educated in [[Roman Catholic]] schools, the priests wanted Doyle to take to a religious career, but he originally wanted to be a [[Veterinarian|veterinary surgeon]]. He studied [[sociology]] and history at [[St Patrick's College, Maynooth]], followed by the [[London College of Printing]], where he earned a diploma in broadcast journalism.
==Broadcasting career==
After graduation, Doyle worked on local radio with BBC Radio Suffolk based in Ipswich, before moving on to [[ITV (TV network)|ITV]] to present the children's show ''[[List of GMTV_programmes#The Disney Club|Disney Club]]'' In 1994, having been head hunted following a chance meeting with a producer from the show at a visit to Alton Towers.
Moving to London, he presented ''[[Tomorrow's World]]'', ''Fasten Your Seatbelt'' and ''Innovation Nation'', and spent six years hosting [[BBC One]]'s ''[[Holiday (TV series)|Holiday]]''. He also had a live music show on London's [[Capital Radio]] every Saturday 8am–11am.
Doyle was a key member of the [[BBC Sport]] team from 2004, anchoring international [[rugby union|rugby]], including the [[Six Nations Championship]], and [[triathlon]], amongst other sports.  He supports [[London Irish]].
In 2004, he formed his own production company Boxer. Its first production was ''The Craig Doyle Show,'' an Irish travel/celebrity program running on RTÉ, and Doyle produced and presented ''Ireland's Richest''.
Released early from his BBC contract, Doyle joined [[ITV Sport]] in February 2008, replacing [[Jim Rosenthal]] by hosting the [[UEFA Champions League]] highlights on ITV1. He also presents [[ITV4]]'s coverage of the [[Isle of Man TT]]. Doyle left Capital Radio at the end of 2008.
Doyle presented ''Ireland's Top Earners'' in 2008, later recalled by John Boland in the ''Irish Independent'' as a programme that came about &quot;just when the country was sliding inexorably into economic ruin and in which Doyle swooned over the wealth that had been amassed by [[Seán Quinn]]&quot; [since bankrupt].&lt;ref&gt;{{cite news|url=http://www.independent.ie/entertainment/tv-radio/john-boland-actually-brennans-tour-wasnt-grand-2939778.html|title=Actually, Brennan's tour wasn't grand|date=19 November 2011|accessdate=19 November 2011|first=John|last=Boland|work=Irish Independent|publisher=Independent News &amp; Media}}&lt;/ref&gt;&lt;ref&gt;{{cite news|url=http://www.rte.ie/news/2012/0116/quinns.html |title=Seán Quinn declared bankrupt at High Court |work=RTÉ News |publisher=Raidió Teilifís Éireann |date=16 January 2012 |accessdate=16 January 2012 |deadurl=yes |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20120117210525/http://www.rte.ie:80/news/2012/0116/quinns.html |archivedate=17 January 2012 |df= }}&lt;/ref&gt;
In April 2010, Doyle returned to Irish TV once again to host his own chat show ''[[Tonight with Craig Doyle]]'' on [[RTÉ One]].&lt;ref&gt;[http://www.rte.ie/tv/programmes/tonight_with_craig_doyle.html &quot;Tonight With Craig Doyle&quot;]. RTÉ.&lt;/ref&gt;
In September 2010 he joined the team on ITV's ''[[Lorraine (TV programme)|Lorraine]]'' as an investigative reporter.&lt;ref&gt;[http://www.itv.com/lorraine/celebrity/lorraineinvestigates/ Lorraine investigates with Craig Doyle] Lorraine, ITV.com, 6 September 2010&lt;/ref&gt;
Doyle presented Irish satirical program ''[[The Panel (Irish TV series)|The Panel]]'' up to 2011. After that he became the presenter for a new live chat show called ''[[The Social (Irish TV series)|The Social]]'' from November 2011, which returned to screens in 2012 as ''[[Craig Doyle Live]]''.
Doyle presented ''Now That's What You Called News'' for RTÉ over the Christmas at the end of 2011.&lt;ref&gt;{{cite news|url=http://www.rte.ie/ten/2011/1128/rtechristmas.html|title=RTÉ announces Christmas highlights|date=28 November 2011|accessdate=28 November 2011|work=RTÉ}}&lt;/ref&gt;
Doyle currently works with BT Sport presenting coverage of Aviva Rugby Union since mid 2013.&lt;ref&gt;http://sport.bt.com/author/craig-doyle-31374087406700&lt;/ref&gt;
Doyle is currently a presenter for BT Sport's coverage of MotoGP since mid 2015.
==Other activities==
Doyle presented the ESAT Young Scientist Exhibition in [[Dublin]], sponsored by [[BT Ireland]] in 2005.
Doyle is prominent in the UK fronting the adverts of double-glazing company [[Everest Windows]]. In Ireland he serves as the face of the UPC cable service adverts.
He is also a face of [[Littlewoods|Littlewoods Ireland]].&lt;ref&gt;{{cite news|url=http://www.rte.ie/ten/2010/0915/morahanc.html|title=Morahan the new face of Littlewoods|date=15 September 2010|accessdate=15 September 2010|work=RTÉ}}&lt;/ref&gt;
==Personal life==
On 7 January 2002, Doyle married his longtime girlfriend Doon, an interior designer from Dublin. The couple have a son Quin, born December 2002, a daughter Muireann, and another son Milo. The family live in Barnamire, Wicklow, and also have a home in [[Kew]], West London. Doyle completed his first triathlon in 2006; a year later he represented Ireland at the World Championships in Hamburg, Germany.&lt;ref&gt;http://www.thelondontriathlon.co.uk/images/PDFs/220Triathlon_Beginners_Guide.pdf&lt;/ref&gt;&lt;ref&gt;[http://www.triathlon.org/results/results/2007_hamburg_bg_triathlon_world_championships/1604/ 2007 Hamburg BG Triathlon World Championships | Triathlon.org&lt;!-- Bot generated title --&gt;]&lt;/ref&gt;

'''Mosiula Faasuka Tatupu''' (April 26, 1955 – February 23, 2010) was a [[National Football League]] [[special teamer]] and [[running back]] from [[American Samoa]] who, during a fifteen-year professional career, played for the [[New England Patriots]] and the [[Los Angeles Rams]]. His tenure with the Patriots lasted from 1978 to 1990.  He made the [[Pro Bowl]] in 1986.&lt;ref&gt;Obituary ''[[New York Times]]'', February 25, 2010.&lt;/ref&gt;
==High school career==
Tatupu was a standout player at [[Punahou School]] where he set many [[Hawaii]] state rushing records.&lt;ref&gt;[http://punahou74.wordpress.com/2009/12/08/punahou-74s-man-in-the-o-men-hall-of-fame-mosiula-tatupu/ Tatupu's Punahou O-Men Hall of Fame Induction Citation]&lt;/ref&gt; He graduated in 1974.&lt;ref&gt;[http://punahou74.wordpress.com/2010/03/03/mosi-tatupu-the-passing-of-a-big-gentleman-both-on-campus-and-in-our-punahou-74-hearts/ Classmates remember Mosi Tatupu]&lt;/ref&gt;&lt;ref&gt;[http://punahou74.wordpress.com/2010/07/05/a-bittersweet-class-reunion-celebrating-the-life-of-mosi-tatupu/ A Bittersweet Class Reunion: Celebrating the Life of Mosi Tatupu]&lt;/ref&gt;
==College career==
Tatupu attended the [[University of Southern California]], playing in the 1978 [[Hula Bowl]] and finished his career with 223 rushing attempts for 1277 yards (5.73 yards per attempt avg.). The [[Mosi Tatupu Award]], given annually to the College Football Special Teams Player of the Year by the Maui Quarterback Club and the Hula Bowl, bears his name.
==NFL career==
Drafted in 1978 by the [[New England Patriots]] (8th round, 215th overall), Tatupu played fullback and became an ace on special teams.  He rushed the ball 612 times for 2,415 yards and 18 touchdowns; in the 1983 season he led the league with 5.5 rushing yards per attempt.  He caught 96 passes for 843 yards and two touchdowns for his career.  His season high for rushing yards came in 1983 with 578 rushing yards and four touchdowns, while in 1984 he set a personal best with 16 catches for 159 yards.  In 1987 against the [[Oakland Raiders|Raiders]] Tatupu threw a 15-yard touchdown to [[Tony Collins (American football)|Tony Collins]].
He was used mostly on special teams kick coverage.  He did have seven kick returns for 56 yards in his career.
==Later life==
Tatupu was the head coach at [[King Philip Regional High School]] in [[Wrentham, Massachusetts]].  Former New England Patriots Center [[Pete Brock (American football)|Pete Brock]] was one of his Assistant Coaches.
Tatupu was most recently the running-backs coach at NCAA Division III school [[Curry College]] in [[Milton, Massachusetts]], a program previously led by former New England Patriot [[Steve Nelson (football)|Steve Nelson]].
Tatupu died in [[Plainville, Massachusetts]]&lt;ref&gt;{{cite web |url=http://espn.go.com/blog/pac10/post/_/id/8252/usc-great-tatupu-dies|title=USC great Tatupu dies|author=Ted Miller|date=2010-02-24|publisher=[[ESPN.com]]|accessdate=2010-02-24}}&lt;/ref&gt;&lt;ref name=starbulletin023210&gt;{{cite web|url=http://www.starbulletin.com/news/bulletin/85178292.html|title=Mosi Tatupu dead at 54|date=February 23, 2010|publisher=Honolulu Star-Bulletin|accessdate=27 May 2010}}&lt;/ref&gt; on February 23, 2010.&lt;ref&gt;{{cite news| url=http://www.boston.com/sports/football/patriots/extra_points/2010/02/mosi_tatupu_die.html | work=The Boston Globe | title=Patriots mourn passing of Mosi Tatupu | first=Matt | last=Pepin | date=February 24, 2010}}&lt;/ref&gt;&lt;ref&gt;{{cite news|url=http://www.latimes.com/sports/football/nfl/wire/sns-ap-fbn-obit-tatupu,0,666181.story |title=Mosi Tatupu, Patriots fan favorite and father of Seahawks linebacker Lofa Tatupu, dies |date=2010-02-24 |work=Los Angeles Times |accessdate=2010-02-24 |deadurl=yes |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20100227023400/http://www.latimes.com/sports/football/nfl/wire/sns-ap-fbn-obit-tatupu,0,666181.story |archivedate=February 27, 2010 }}&lt;/ref&gt; The cause of death was a [[heart attack]]; in 2014, using brain tissue preserved from his 2010 autopsy, he was posthumously diagnosed with [[chronic traumatic encephalopathy]] by the CTE Center at [[Boston University School of Medicine]].&lt;ref name=BG012715&gt;Kay Lazar, [https://www.bostonglobe.com/metro/2015/01/26/football-warrior-long-descent-finally-explained/0xf7bJSXnb2eLsKY0234BN/story.html Years of battering took toll on 1980s Patriots star Mosi Tatupu], ''Boston Globe'', January 27, 2015, accessed October 6, 2015.&lt;/ref&gt;
==Family==
His son [[Lofa Tatupu]] played linebacker for the [[University of Southern California]] and middle [[linebacker]] for the [[Seattle Seahawks]].{{ref|son}}Nephew Joe Tuipala also a NFL linebacker from 1999-2005.
==In pop culture==
In ''[[The Simpsons]]'' episode &quot;[[Treehouse of Horror III]]&quot; Mosi Tatupu's name is used during the &quot;King Homer&quot; segment. This segment is a parody of the 1933 film ''[[King Kong (1933 film)|King Kong]]''. During this segment, the character of the chief of Ape Island is shown to say &quot;Mosi Tatupu, Mosi Tatupu&quot;, which in their language means &quot;the blue-haired woman will make a fine sacrifice&quot;. The blue-haired woman is Marge Simpson who is playing Fay Wray to Homer's King Kong. One of the most popular players to play for the New England Patriots, Tatupu even had his own section of fans at Foxboro Stadium, &quot;Mosi's Mooses,&quot; who all adorned moose heads and continually chanted his name throughout every game he played at home.

The '''Mastín Español''' or '''Spanish Mastiff''', is a giant [[breed]] of dog, originating in Spain, originally bred to be a [[guard dog]] whose specialized purpose is to be a [[Livestock guardian dog]] protecting flocks (and occasionally herds) from [[Gray wolf|wolves]] and other [[predator]]s.  The [[Mountain dog]] type has a heavier coat.
==Historical context==
[[File:ИСПАНСКИЙ МАСТИФ.JPG|thumb|right|Brindle colored Spanish Mastiff.]]
[[Transhumance]] in Spain is very ancient, like the primitive populations of those lands and, consequently, the Mastiff-Transhumance binomial. In the [[Iron Age]] of the [[Castile (historical region)|Castilian]] Plateau it found skeletons of dogs of enormous dimensions. Also is assumed that already in the [[Neolithic]] existed molossers in [[Central Europe]].{{fact|date=October 2016}}
In different parts of the globe, appeared simultaneously various types of cattle dogs of molosser type, one of these places was Spain considering the natural characteristics of the peninsula. Specifically the Spanish Mastiff was originated in the territories of [[Asturias]], [[Cantabria]], [[Province of León|León]] and [[Province of Zamora|Zamora]].&lt;ref&gt;[http: //listadoderazasdeperrosygatos.blogspot.com/2012/10/raza-mastin-espanol.html &quot;Raza de Perro Mastín Español (Spanish Mastiff)&quot; listadoderazasdeperrosygatos]&lt;/ref&gt;
Th [[Prehistoric Europe|Indo-Europeans]], some groups composed of warriors herders and nomadic transhumans, led to large herd molossers dogs the valleys and areas conducive to grass. In the seasons of transhumance it had to walk about thirty kilometers or more per day, which gathered other nine for grazing; without the ebb and continued during monitoring.&lt;ref&gt;[http://www.mastinespanol.org/mastin_espanol_raza.htm The breed - History&quot;, mastinespañol.org]&lt;/ref&gt;
With the birth of the farming system, the dogs became indispensable. There was probably external influences acting on the base structure of the native dogs. Through centuries of selection and specialization, and thanks to this ecological ring pressent in many countries of the world (man, sheep, dog and wolf), it gave life to a specimen of a physical and a useful dog.
After, in [[Middle Ages|Medieval times]], during centuries, the Mastín Español has accompanied the herds of transhumans [[sheep]]s that ran cañadas reales crossing from north to south Spain, defending the cattle of attack of [[wolf|wolves]] and other vermin; the Mastín had the protection of carlancas or carrancas, chunky metal necklaces with skewers. Its function was primarily protective, unlike its fellow [[Carea (type)|Carea Dogs]], whose function is grazing, driving the herds in response to indications of the shepherd &lt;ref&gt;{{cite web |author=Antón Burgos, Francisco Javier |title=Herding dogs in Spain. Origins and functionality|url=http://www.aepme.org/joomla/index.php/articulos-sobre-la-raza/225-perros-de-pastoreo-en-espana-fco-javier-anton-burgos|publisher=Spanish Association of Mastín Español Dog (AEPME) |date=2014 |accessdate=July 11, 2015}}&lt;/ref&gt; In some places it is known as ''perro merinero'' by accompany the [[Merino Sheep|Merino]] sheep breed.
The first breed standard of the Mastín was made by the [[Fédération Cynologique Internationale|FCI]] in 1946. In 1981 was created the Asociación Española del Perro Mastín Español, who organized a breeding program looking for the kind of large and strong mastiff of the past times, and drafted a new breed standard focused on recovering the old cattle dogs, fit as pets, and as guard dog and defense.&lt;ref&gt;[http://www.miperro.info/2014/09/el-patron-racial-del-mastin-espanol.html]&lt;/ref&gt;
==Appearance==
The Spanish Mastiff is a very large and powerful dog, similar in appearance to the other Mastiff breeds.   They have a large powerful head and serious and vigilant expression
Males in this breed are {{convert|70|to|85|cm|in}} tall at the withers, and range from {{convert|50|to|70|kg|lb}}. Females are at least {{convert|65|cm|in}}, and weigh {{convert|40|to|60|kg|lb}}.&lt;ref&gt;{{citation|url=http://www.dogbreedslist.info/all-dog-breeds/Spanish-Mastiff.html|title=The Spanish Mastiff}}&lt;/ref&gt;
It has small eyes and drop ears resembling triangles. This dog's coat is most often fawn-colored, but can also be brindle, black or 'wolf' colored. Reddish tones indicate miscegenation
==Temperament==
[[File:Mastspagn3.jpg|thumb|right|A couple of Spanish Mastiffs]]
This noble giant is aloof, dignified, calm and intelligent.{{citation needed|date=April 2013}} It is devoted to its family and may politely accept strangers if it has been socialized properly, although it will be wary of them. It can be aggressive toward other dogs.{{citation needed|date=April 2013}} The Spanish Mastiff may be a less-than-ideal pet in urban situations, where its booming voice and massive size could be problematic. It is a wonderful protector of its home and family.  And an ideal protector of herds and flocks from wolf predation.&lt;ref&gt;{{cite web |url=http://www.wyadmb.com/2011%20Projects/Transferring%20successful%20Old%20World%20livestock%20protection%20dog%20traditions%20to%20areas%20of%20large%20carnivore%20occupancy%20in%20the%20United%20States.doc |title=Transferring successful Old World livestock protection dog traditions to areas of large carnivore occupancy in the United States (Livestock Protection Dog International Research Project Report) |first1=Jim |last1=Urbigkit |first2=Cat |last2=Urbigkit |first3=Yolanda, Editor |last3=Cortez  |publisher=Wyoming Wool Growers Association, Wyoming Animal Damage Management Board |format=MSWord doc |accessdate=February 27, 2017 |pages=1-46}}&lt;/ref&gt;
Socialization and training should begin early to ensure this dog a stable and reliable pet. Supervised exposure in puppy-hood to a variety of unfamiliar but non-threatening dogs will help dampen a tendency to aggression toward other dogs.{{citation needed|date=April 2013}} The breed is quite alert and food motivated but can bore easily; training must be consistent and firm but gentle. Once the trainer has established the dog's respect as leader, the Spanish Mastiff will be an extremely loyal pet.{{citation needed|date=April 2013}}
==Exercise==
This dog is more inclined to lumber than gallop, but it can move quite rapidly when necessary. A long daily walk will be sufficient, although it will appreciate a fenced area where it can exercise at its own rate.{{citation needed|date=April 2013}}
==Representatives dogs==
* [[Las Meninas]] by [[Diego Velázquez]] features an impressive example of the breed.
* Actor [[Viggo Mortensen]] has, by a gift when he was in León, both a Carea Leonés and a Leonese Mastiff, named &quot;Aragorn&quot; and &quot;Alatriste&quot;, named of characters he played in his movies.&lt;ref&gt;[http://www.escaparatedemascotas.com/famosos/viggo-mortensen/ &quot;Viggo Mortensen&quot; escaparatedemascotas.com]&lt;/ref&gt;

The '''Galt House''' is a 25-story, 1300-room [[hotel]] in [[Louisville, Kentucky]] established in 1972.  It is named for a nearby historic hotel erected in 1837 and demolished in 1921. The Galt House is the city's only hotel on the [[Ohio River]].
==Original Galt House==
[[Image:BullNelsonShooting.jpg|thumb|left|[[Union Army|Union]] Gen. [[Jefferson C. Davis]] shoots Union Gen. [[William &quot;Bull&quot; Nelson]] at the Galt House in 1862]]
The Galt House was, in the early 19th century, the residence of Dr. W.C. Galt.  The house was located at the corner of Second and Main Street.
In 1834, the first instance of the Galt House as a hotel was established and in 1835 was opened by Col. Ariss Throckmorton as a 60-room hotel on the northeast corner of Second and Main streets in Louisville.  During the nineteenth century, The Galt House was acclaimed as Louisville's best hotel. Many noted people stayed at the original Galt House, including [[Jefferson Davis]], [[Charles Dickens]], [[Abraham Lincoln]] and [[Ulysses S. Grant]].{{Citation needed|date=September 2007}}
During the [[American Civil War|Civil War]], the Galt House was utilized for meetings of [[Union Army|Union]] generals. In September 1862, it was the scene of an unusual murder, when General [[Jefferson C. Davis]] (not to be confused with [[Confederate States Army|Confederate]] President [[Jefferson Davis]]) shot Union General [[William &quot;Bull&quot; Nelson]] after a dispute.
According to a historical marker for the original Galt House, in March 1864, Generals [[Ulysses S. Grant]] and [[William Tecumseh Sherman]] met at the Galt House to plan the invasion that led to the [[Atlanta Campaign|successful capture of Atlanta, Georgia]] and [[Sherman's March to the Sea]].  As of 2014, this claim has fallen into dispute.&lt;ref&gt;{{cite news |last=Bullard |first=Gabe |date=2014-03-16 |title=No, Ulysses S. Grant and William Tecumseh Sherman Didn't Plan the March to the Sea in Louisville |url=http://wfpl.org/post/no-ulysses-s-grant-and-william-tecumseh-sherman-didnt-plan-march-sea-louisville |location=Louisville, Kentucky |publisher=[[WFPL]] |accessdate=2014-06-14 }}&lt;/ref&gt;
What was to be the first Galt House burned down in 1865.  Four years later, in 1869, a larger Galt House was established on the corner of First and Main streets.  Known as being the center of Louisville's social community during this time, the hotel subsequently fell on hard times in the next 50 years and was closed in 1919 due to financial difficulties.  Soon after, in 1921, the building was demolished.
==Current Galt House==
Over a half a century later, in 1972, the Galt House Hotel was reestablished by developer Al J Schneider as part of Louisville's Riverfront Urban Renewal Project.  The West (RIVUE) Tower is 25 stories high and features deluxe guest rooms.  An East (Suite) Tower was added in 1984.  It offers 650 suites, including waterfront balcony suites and waterfront apartments.  At nearly 1,300 guest rooms, Galt House Hotel is the largest hotel in [[Kentucky]]. It has 128,000 square feet of meeting space, including 53 meeting rooms, two ballrooms and an exhibit hall.  On-site there are six restaurants, a business and shipping center, a spa and salon, a barbershop and retail shops.  Every year since 1986, the statewide [[Governor's Cup (academics)|Governor's Cup]] has been held at the Galt House Hotel.  It is the Official Hotel of Churchill Downs and the Kentucky Derby.
Al J Schneider's daughter, Mary Moseley, became President and CEO of the company and has led a more than $70 million renovation of the Galt House Hotel.  Under her leadership, many updates and renovations have been completed, including the addition of a 3-story glass-jewel Conservatory that links the Suite and RIVUE Towers over Fourth Street. The {{convert|10000|sqft|m2|adj=on}} conservatory is three stories in height and enclosed by steel and glass. It features a cafe, a cocktail lounge and gathering area, an [[aviary]] and [[greenhouse]] space on one level with large trees and [[foliage]]. The Grand Ballroom and Archibald Cochran Ballroom, as well as guest rooms and meeting rooms were renovated. The Conservatory, Club 360 Rooftop Fitness Center, the Rooftop Garden and Terrace, and RIVUE Restaurant and Lounge offer views of [[downtown Louisville]] and the [[Ohio River]]. A newly constructed pedestrian bridge crossing Main Street connects the Galt House and Riverfront Plaza Towers with the rest of the Downtown Louisville skybridge system.

      <format>text/x-wiki</format>
      <text xml:space="preserve">'''Mithridates''' (in [[Greek language|Greek]] Mιθριδάτης; lived 4th century BCE), son of [[Ariobarzanes I of Cius|Ariobarzanes]] prince of [[Cius]], is mentioned by [[Xenophon]]{{r|xen1_8.8.4}} as having betrayed his father, and the same circumstance is alluded to by [[Aristotle]].{{r|aris_5.10}}
He may or may not be the same [[Mithridates (soldier)|Mithradates]] who accompanied the younger [[Cyrus the Younger|Cyrus]], or the same [[Mithradates, Satrap of Cappadocia|Mithradates]] mentioned by Xenophon{{r|xen2_7.8.25}} as [[satrap]] of [[Cappadocia]] and [[Lycaonia]] in the late 5th century BCE.
During the [[Revolt of the Satraps|Satraps' Revolt]] in the 360s BCE, Mithridates tricked [[Datames]] to believe in him, but in the end arranged Datames' murder in 362 BCE. Similarly, Mithridates gave his own father [[Ariobarzanes of Phrygia]] to the hands of the Persian overlord, so Ariobarzanes was crucified in 362 BCE.
[[Demosthenes]] speaks of Ariobarzanes and his three sons having been lately made [[Athens|Athenian]] citizens.{{r|dem1}} - as signal of sympathy in the revolt effort, Athens made Ariobarzanes and three of his sons citizens of Athens. Mithradates was possibly one of those sons.
In 363 BCE already, [[Ariobarzanes II of Cius|Ariobarzanes II]] (possibly Mithridates' son) made himself master of the family fiefdom of Cius in [[Mysia]].{{r|diod_15.90}} This Mithradates may therefore have died in 363 BCE, but the date is not recorded and only comes from later reconstructions of the succession in the dynasty.
Otherwise, this Mithradates may well be the same man as the elderly [[Mithridates II of Cius]] who held Cius in Mysia between 337 and 302 BCE, being said to be an old man at that time.

'''Anne V. &quot;Anna&quot; Quayle'''{{cn|reason = Source for name 'Anne V.'?|date=December 2016}} (born 6 October 1932, [[Birmingham, England|Birmingham]]) is an English actress. Her parents were actor Douglas Quayle&lt;ref&gt;''Playbill Magazine'', NYC, Sam S. Shubert Theatre, vol. 1, no. 23, 3 June 1963; Quayle's &quot;Who's Who in the Cast&quot; for ''[[Stop the World - I Want to Get Off]]''&lt;/ref&gt; and the former Kathleen Parke.
==Career==
Quayle was educated at the [[Convent of Jesus and Mary Language College|Convent of Jesus and Mary High School]], [[Harlesden]].
She has appeared on film, on stage and on television. Her film appearances include ''[[Smashing Time]]'' (1967), a short but memorable scene that she shares with [[John Lennon]] in ''[[A Hard Day's Night (film)|A Hard Day's Night]]'' (1964), the [[German Expressionism|German expressionist]] sequence of ''[[Casino Royale (1967 film)|Casino Royale]]'' (1967) and in the musical ''[[Chitty Chitty Bang Bang (film)|Chitty Chitty Bang Bang]]'' (1968) as [[Baroness Bomburst]]. In 1963, Quayle appeared on Broadway in the original production of ''[[Stop the World - I Want to Get Off]]'' opposite [[Anthony Newley]], for which she won a [[Tony Award]] for Best Supporting Musical Actress. Other television work includes the comedy drama ''[[Mapp and Lucia]]'', the children's science fiction series ''[[The Georgian House]]'' and ''[[Grange Hill]]'' where she played the role of [[Kate Monroe|Mrs Monroe]] from 1990–94. In 1973, she appeared as a regular panellist on the popular [[BBC2]] panel game show ''[[What's My Line?]]'' {{Citation needed|date=June 2012}}

  <page>
    <title>Alonso de Castillo Solórzano</title>
    <ns>0</ns>
    <id>2336567</id>
    <revision>
      <id>770822461</id>
      <parentid>750679900</parentid>
      <timestamp>2017-03-17T20:06:18Z</timestamp>
      <contributor>
        <username>DavidBrooks-AWB</username>
        <id>20962961</id>
      </contributor>
      <comment>+EB1911 cite, other fixes and WLs using [[Project:AWB|AWB]]</comment>
      <model>wikitext</model>
      <format>text/x-wiki</format>
      <text xml:space="preserve">'''Alonso de Castillo''' (1584?, probably in [[Tordesillas]], [[Valladolid (province)|Valladolid]]{{snd}}1647?, probably in [[Palermo]]) was a [[Spain|Spanish]] novelist and playwright.
He is said to have been [[Baptism|baptized]] October 1, 1584. He is next heard of at [[Madrid]] in 1619 as a man of literary tastes. While in the service of the [[Pierre de Villars|Marquis de Villars]], he issued his first work, ''Donaires del Parnaso'' (1624–1625), two volumes of humorous poems; his ''Tardes entretenidas'' (1625) and ''Jornadas alegres'' (1626) proved that he was a novelist by vocation.&lt;ref name=&quot;EB1911&quot;&gt;{{EB1911|inline=y|wstitle=Castillo Solórzano, Alonso de|volume=5|page=476|first=James|last=Fitzmaurice-Kelly|authorlink=James Fitzmaurice-Kelly}}&lt;/ref&gt;
Shortly afterwards he joined the household of the [[Pedro Fajardo, 5th Marquis of Los Vélez|Marquis de los Vélez]], [[Viceroy]] of [[Kingdom of Valencia|Valencia]], and published in quick succession three clever [[picaresque novel]]s: ''La Niña de los embustes, Teresa de Manzanares'' (1634), ''Las Aventuras del Bachiller Trapaza'' (1637), and a continuation entitled ''La Garduña de Sevilla y Anzuelo de las bolsas'' (1642). To these shrewd cynical stories he owes his reputation.&lt;ref name=&quot;EB1911&quot;/&gt;
He followed the Marquis de los Vélez in his disastrous campaign in [[Catalonia]] (the [[Reapers' War]]) and accompanied him to [[Rome]], where the defeated general was sent as ambassador. Castillo Solórzano's death occurred before 1648, but the exact date is uncertain. His prolonged absence from Madrid prevented him from writing as copiously for the stage as he would otherwise have done; but he was popular as a playwright both at home and abroad. His ''Marqués del Cigarral'' and ''El Mayorazgo figurón'' are the sources respectively of [[Paul Scarron|Scarron]]'s ''Don Jophet d'Arménie'' and ''L'Héritier ridicule''. Among his numerous remaining works may be mentioned ''Las harpías en Madrid'' (1633), ''Fiestas del Jardín'' (1634), ''Los Alivios de Casandra'' (1640) and the posthumous ''Quinta de Laurel'' (1649); the witty observation of these books forms a singular contrast to the prim devotion of his ''Sagrario de Valencia'' (1635).&lt;ref name=&quot;EB1911&quot;/&gt;

'''''Tapinoma''''' (from [[Greek language|Greek]] ''ταπείνωμα'' low position) is a [[genus]] of [[ant]]s that belongs to the [[subfamily]] [[Dolichoderinae]]. The genus currently comprises 74&lt;ref name=&quot;AWTapinoma&quot;/&gt; described species distributed worldwide in [[tropical]] and [[temperate regions]]. Members of are generalized foragers, nesting in a wide variety of habitats, ranging from grasslands, open fields, woodlands, to inside buildings. The majority of species nest in the ground under objects such as stones or tree logs, other species build nests under bark of logs and stumps, in plant cavities, insect galls or refuse piles.&lt;ref&gt;{{Cite journal | last1 = Sharaf | first1 = M. | last2 = Aldawood | first2 = A. | last3 = Elhawagry | first3 = M. | doi = 10.3897/zookeys.212.3325 | title = A new ant species of the genus Tapinoma (Hymenoptera, Formicidae) from Saudi Arabia with a key to the Arabian species | journal = ZooKeys | volume = 212 | issue = 212 | pages = 35–43 | year = 2012 | pmid =  22933848| pmc =3428702 }}&lt;/ref&gt;
[[File: Formicidae - Tapinoma species.JPG |thumb|240px|right|''Tapinoma'' species with Wax scales]]

'''''Kilowatt''''' is an album by jazz fusion guitarist [[Kazumi Watanabe]], originally released on audio cassette in 1989. In 1991 it was released again on cassette, CD and LP.
==Track listing==
All tracks by Kazumi Watanabe except where noted.

#&quot;Capri&quot; - 4:10
#&quot;No One&quot; (Watanabe/Brunel) - 5:33
#&quot;Jive&quot; (Watanabe/Brunel) - 3:48
#&quot;Papyrus&quot; - 4:50
#&quot;Sunspin&quot; - 5:15
#&quot;Pretty Soon&quot; (Brunel) - 5:37
#&quot;Bernard&quot; (Brunel) - 4:42
#&quot;Dolphin Dance&quot; ([[Herbie Hancock]]) - 6:59
#&quot;Good Night Machines&quot; (Watanabe/Moraz/Brunel) - 6:18
==Personnel==
* [[Kazumi Watanabe]] - guitars, synth guitars, keyboards
* [[Bunny Brunel]] - bass, synth bass, keyboards
* John Wackerman - drums, synth drums, electric vibes
===Additional Musicians===
* [[Wayne Shorter]] - sax (2, 8)
* [[Patrick Moraz]] - keyboards (1, 2, 4, 8, 10)
* [[Alex Acuna]] - percussion (2, 3, 4, 5, 7, 8)

      <text xml:space="preserve">{{Infobox Bridge

|image         = Knight Street Bridge.jpg
|carries       = 4-6 lanes of [[Knight Street]], pedestrians and bicycles
|crosses       = [[Fraser River|North Arm Fraser River]]
|locale        = [[Richmond, British Columbia|Richmond]]&lt;br&gt;[[Vancouver]]

|maint=[[TransLink (British Columbia)|TransLink]]

|open      = 1974

The '''[[Knight Street]] Bridge''' is a [[cantilever bridge]] which spans the North Arm of the [[Fraser River]] in [[British Columbia]], connecting [[Vancouver]] and [[Richmond, British Columbia|Richmond]], and serving as a feeder route for [[List of British Columbia provincial highways|Highways]] [[British Columbia Highway 91|91]] and [[British Columbia Highway 99|99]] to its south. It is located to the east of the [[Oak Street Bridge]]. Besides spanning the river, the bridge also provides access to [[Mitchell Island]]. The bridge has a length of 1436 metres&lt;ref name=&quot;TH&quot;&gt;{{cite web |url=http://www.th.gov.bc.ca/publications/frontiertofreeway/frontiertofreeway.pdf |title=Frontier to Freeway: A short illustrated history of the roads in British Columbia}}&lt;/ref&gt; and has clearances of 12.2 by 79.2 metres over the north channel, and 20.1 by 109.7 metres for the south channel. The northern section carries six lanes of traffic, while the southern section carries four. 
The bridge has the distinction of having the most bridge motor vehicle accidents in BC. In addition, the bridge's interchange with Marine Drive is in the top three intersections for motor vehicle accidents in BC.&lt;ref&gt;[http://www.canada.com/vancouversun/news/westcoastnews/story.html?id=29765c8a-1397-479d-ab35-2f1a20c41f8b Accident-prone Metro home to all top 10 crash sites], ''Vancouver Sun'', November 12, 2009. Accessed online January 20, 2011.&lt;/ref&gt;
[[TransLink (British Columbia)|TransLink]], the regional transportation authority, is responsible for the bridge.&lt;ref&gt;[http://www.translink.ca/en/Getting-Around/Driving/Traffic-Cameras/Bridges-and-Tunnels/Knight-St-Bridge.aspx Knight St Bridge], TransLink&lt;/ref&gt;
==History==
The bridge was built to replace an obsolete span linking the south end of Fraser Street with No. 5 Road in Richmond via [[Mitchell Island]]. The Fraser Street Bridge was a through truss built in 1905 with a swing span on the northern side of Mitchell Island. The channel was difficult to navigate, making collisions with ships and barges routine. The height of the Knight Street bridge alleviated this problem. 
The construction of the Knight Street Bridge took 5 years, costing about $15 million including the approaches. Electric heating cables were installed in the deck to minimize the use of de-icing salt in the winter.&lt;ref name=&quot;VanHist&quot;&gt;{{cite web |url=http://www.vancouverhistory.ca/chronology1974.htm |title=The History of Metropolitan Vancouver - 1974 Chronology}}&lt;/ref&gt; The bridge also carries a water pipe and a gas pipe, with the former being the only water supply to Mitchell Island at the time.&lt;ref name=&quot;watermain&quot;&gt;{{cite web |url=http://www.richmond.ca/__shared/assets/061200_item251214.pdf |title=City of Richmond: Report to Committee re: Knight Street Bridge Watermain}}&lt;/ref&gt; The bridge opened on January 15, 1974, and the [[Fraser Street Bridge]] was dismantled the next month.&lt;ref name=&quot;VanHist&quot;/&gt;
On January 15, 2000 the boom of a mobile crane transported on a barge named ''T.L. Sharpe'', towed by the ''Sea Cap XII'', struck the underside of the Knight Street Bridge at 1:45 PM, damaging the bridge and the fixtures secured underneath its deck. The impact caused the boom to bend and the crane to slide off the barge and sink, and the bridge was closed to traffic for about 48 hours.&lt;ref&gt;{{cite web |url=http://www.tsb.gc.ca/eng/rapports-reports/marine/2000/m00w0005/m00w0005.asp |title=Transportation Safety Board of Canada - MARINE REPORTS - 2000 - M00W0005}}&lt;/ref&gt; Water supply to Mitchell Island via the bridge was shut down for 25 days, and an emergency bypass water supply from Vancouver was installed.&lt;ref name=&quot;watermain&quot;/&gt; The incident prompted the City of Richmond to install a second water main to Mitchell Island in 2002.&lt;ref&gt;{{cite web |url=http://www.richmond.ca/__shared/assets/Annual_Report_20025953.pdf |title=City of Richmond: 2002 Annual Report}}&lt;/ref&gt;

'''TVP1''' ('''TVP Jeden''', ''Program I Telewizji Polskiej'', ''&quot;Jedynka&quot;'') is a television channel owned by [[Telewizja Polska|TVP]] (Telewizja Polska S.A.), [[Poland]]'s national public broadcaster. It was the first Polish channel to be broadcast and remains one of the most popular today. TVP1 was launched August 1939/25 October 1952 (tests), January 1953 (regular programming).
[[Image:TVP1 HD logo.svg|thumb|right|Logo of TVP1 HD]]
==TVP1 HD==
In addition to its [[standard definition television|SD]] broadcast, a [[High-definition television|HD]] version of TVP1 is also available. Test broadcast started in January 2011, later in June 2012 official broadcast of TVP1 HD began with the coverage of the [[UEFA Euro 2012]].&lt;ref&gt;{{cite web |url=http://www.tvp.pl/o-tvp/centrum-prasowe/komunikaty-prasowe/tvp-rozpoczyna-cyfrowa-emisje-programow-tvp1-oraz-tvp2-w-wysokiej-rozdzielczosci-hd/7407293 |title= TVP rozpoczyna cyfrową emisję programów TVP1 oraz TVP2 w wysokiej rozdzielczości (HD)  |publisher=tvp.pl |date=18 May 2012}}&lt;/ref&gt;

* ''Polityka przy kawie'' (Political quarter of an hour) - morning political talk show
* ''Warto rozmawiać'' (It is worth to talk) - controversial talk show, accused of right-wing spinning, hosted by Jan Pospieszalski
* ''Chodzi o pieniądze'' (It's about money) - economic magazine hosted by Jacek Łęski
* ''Magazyn śledczy Anity Gargas'' - investigative magazine

    <title>Flight envelope</title>
    <ns>0</ns>
    <id>2336592</id>
    <revision>
      <id>749680097</id>
      <parentid>728309439</parentid>
      <timestamp>2016-11-15T17:15:53Z</timestamp>
      <contributor>
        <username>GreenC bot</username>
        <id>27823944</id>
      </contributor>
      <minor />
      <comment>1 archive template merged to {{[[template:webarchive|webarchive]]}} ([[User:Green_Cardamom/Webarchive_template_merge|WAM]])</comment>
      <model>wikitext</model>
      <format>text/x-wiki</format>
      <text xml:space="preserve">{{Refimprove|date=June 2009}}
[[Image:PerformanceEnvelope.gif|300px|thumb|Flight envelope diagram.]]
In [[aerodynamics]], the '''flight envelope''', '''service envelope''', or '''performance envelope''' of an [[aircraft]] refers to the capabilities of a design in terms of [[airspeed]] and [[Load factor (aeronautics)|load factor]] or altitude.&lt;ref&gt;[http://ecfr.gpoaccess.gov/cgi/t/text/text-idx?type=simple;c=ecfr;cc=ecfr;sid=a8f38006e777ba46ba8000f7c2fe6641;region=DIV1;q1=23.335;rgn=div8;view=text;idno=14;node=14%3A1.0.1.3.10.3.70.8 §23.333 Flight envelope]&lt;/ref&gt;&lt;ref&gt;[http://www.access.gpo.gov/ecfr/graphics/pdfs/ec28se91.001.pdf Flight envelope - diagram] {{webarchive |url=https://web.archive.org/web/20100601204507/http://www.access.gpo.gov/ecfr/graphics/pdfs/ec28se91.001.pdf |date=June 1, 2010 }}&lt;/ref&gt; The term is somewhat loosely applied, and can also refer to other measurements such as maneuverability. When a plane is pushed, for instance by diving it at high speeds, it is said to be flown &quot;outside the envelope&quot;, something considered rather dangerous.
Flight envelope is one of a number of related terms that are all used in a similar fashion. It is perhaps the most common term because it is the oldest, first being used in the early days of test flying. It is closely related to more modern terms known as '''extra power''' and a '''doghouse plot''' which are different ways of describing a flight envelope. In addition, the term has been widened in scope outside the field of engineering, to refer to the strict limits in which an event will take place or more generally to the '''predictable behavior''' of a given phenomenon or situation, and hence, its &quot;flight envelope&quot; .
==Extra power==
Extra power, or ''specific excess power'',&lt;ref name=&quot;MFHap&quot;/&gt; is a very basic method of determining an aircraft's flight envelope. It is easily calculated, but as a downside does not tell very much about the actual performance of the aircraft at different altitudes. 
Choosing any particular set of parameters will generate the needed power for a particular aircraft for those conditions. For instance a [[Cessna 150]] at 2,500&amp;nbsp;ft (800 m) altitude and 90&amp;nbsp;mph (140&amp;nbsp;km/h) speed needs about 60&amp;nbsp;hp (45&amp;nbsp;kW) to fly straight and level. The C150 is normally equipped with a 100&amp;nbsp;hp (75&amp;nbsp;kW) engine, so in this particular case the plane has 40&amp;nbsp;hp (30&amp;nbsp;kW) of extra power. In overall terms this is very little extra power, 60% of the engine's output is already used up just keeping the plane in the air. The leftover 40&amp;nbsp;hp (30&amp;nbsp;kW) is all that the aircraft has to maneuver with, meaning it can climb, turn, or speed up only a small amount. To put this in perspective, the C150 could not maintain a 2[[g-force|''g'']] (20&amp;nbsp;m/s²) turn, which would require 120&amp;nbsp;hp (or somewhat more) under the same conditions.
For the same conditions a [[fighter aircraft]] might require considerably more power due to their wings being inefficient at low speeds, for argument's sake it might require 10,000&amp;nbsp;hp (7.5 MW). However modern jet engines can provide considerable power, the equivalent of 50,000&amp;nbsp;hp (37 MW) typically. With this amount of extra power the aircraft can achieve very high maximum [[rate of climb]], even climb straight up, make powerful continual maneuvers, or fly at very high speeds.
==Doghouse plot==
[[Image:AltitudeEnvelopeText.GIF|thumb|Altitude envelope]]
[[Image:TurnRateEnvelope.GIF|thumb|Turn rate envelope]]
A doghouse plot generally shows the relation between speed at level flight and altitude, although other variables are also possible. It takes more effort to make than an extra power calculation, but in turn provides much more information such as ideal flight altitude. The plot typically looks something like an upside-down U and is commonly referred to as a doghouse plot due to its resemblance to a doghouse. The diagram on the right shows a very simplified plot which shall be used to explain the general shape of the plot.
The outer edges of the diagram, the envelope, show the possible conditions that the aircraft can reach in straight and level flight. For instance, the aircraft described by the black altitude envelope on the right can fly at altitudes up to about 52,000 feet, at which point the thinner air means it can no longer climb. The aircraft can also fly at up to Mach 1.1 at sea level, but no faster. This outer surface of the curve represents the ''zero-extra-power condition''. All of the area under the curve represents conditions that the plane can fly at with power to spare, for instance, this aircraft can fly at Mach 0.5 at 30,000 feet while using less than full power.
In the case of high-performance aircraft, including fighters, this &quot;1-g&quot; line showing straight-and-level flight is augmented with additional lines showing the maximum performance at various g loadings. In the diagram at right, the green line represents, 2-g, the blue line 3-g, and so on. The [[F-16 Fighting Falcon]] has a very small area just below Mach 1 and close to sea level where it can maintain a 9-g turn.
Flying outside the envelope is possible, since it represents the straight-and-level condition only. For instance diving the aircraft allows higher speeds, using gravity as a source of additional power. Likewise higher altitude can be reached by first speeding up and then going ballistic, a maneuver known as a [[zoom climb]].
===Stalling speed===
All [[fixed-wing aircraft]] have a minimum speed at which they can maintain level flight, the [[stall speed]] (left limit line in the diagram). As the aircraft gains altitude the stall speed increases; since the wing is not growing any larger the only way to support the aircraft's weight with less air is to increase speed. While the exact numbers will vary widely from aircraft to aircraft, the nature of this relationship is typically the same; plotted on a graph of speed (x-axis) vs. altitude (y-axis) it forms a diagonal line.
===Service ceiling===
Inefficiencies in the wings also make this line &quot;tilt over&quot; with increased altitude, until it becomes horizontal and no additional speed will result in increased altitude. This maximum altitude is known as the [[service ceiling]] (top limit line in the diagram), and is often quoted for aircraft performance. The area where the altitude for a given speed can no longer be increased at level flight is known as ''zero rate of climb'' and is caused by the [[Lift (force)|lift]] of the aircraft getting smaller at higher altitudes, until it no longer exceeds [[gravity]].
===Top speed===
The right side of the graph represents the maximum speed of the aircraft. This is typically sloped in the same manner as the stall line due to air resistance getting lower at higher altitudes, up to the point where an increase in altitude no longer increases the maximum speed due to lack of oxygen to feed the engines.
The power needed varies almost linearly with altitude, but the nature of [[drag (physics)|drag]] means that it varies with the square of speed—in other words it is typically easier to go higher than faster, up to the altitude where lack of oxygen for the engines starts to play a significant role.
==Velocity vs. load factor chart==
[[File:F-104A flight envelope.jpg|thumb|upright=1.3|A V-n diagram showing V&lt;sub&gt;S&lt;/sub&gt; (stall speed at 1G), V&lt;sub&gt;C&lt;/sub&gt; (corner/maneuver speed) and V&lt;sub&gt;D&lt;/sub&gt; (dive speed)]]
A chart of velocity versus load factor (or V-n diagram) is another way of showing limits of aircraft performance. It shows how much load factor can be safely achieved at different airspeeds.&lt;ref name=&quot;MFHap&quot;&gt;Sinclair, Edward J. [http://www.usarmyaviation.com/studyguides/index.php?folder=Documents/General%20Studyguides&amp;download=Maneuvering%20Flight%20Handbook%2024%20MAR%2005.pdf &quot;The Army Aviator's Handbook for Maneuvering Flight and Power Management&quot;]. p. 25. ''[[United States Army Aviation Branch]]'', 24 March 2005. Accessed: 6 January 2011.&lt;/ref&gt;
==Sidenotes==
Although it is easy to compare aircraft on simple numbers such as maximum speed or service ceiling, an examination of the flight envelope will reveal far more information. Generally a design with a larger area under the curve will have better all-around performance. This is because when the plane is not flying at the edges of the envelope, its extra power will be greater, and that means more power for things like climbing or maneuvering. [[General aviation]] aircraft have very small flight envelopes, with speeds ranging from perhaps 50 to 200&amp;nbsp;mph, whereas the extra power available to modern fighter aircraft result in huge flight envelopes with many times the area. As a tradeoff however, military aircraft often have a higher stalling speed. As a result of this the landing speed is also higher.
== &quot;Pushing the envelope&quot; ==
{{redirect|Pushing the envelope|the album|Pushing the Envelope (album)}}
This phrase is used to refer to an aircraft being taken to, and perhaps beyond, its designated altitude and speed limits.&lt;ref name=&quot;mqPush&quot;&gt;Quinion, Michael. [http://www.worldwidewords.org/qa/qa-pus1.htm Push the envelope] ''World Wide Words''. Accessed: 6 January 2011.&lt;/ref&gt; By extension, this phrase may be used to mean testing other limits, either within aerospace or in other fields e.g. [[Plus ultra (motto)]].&lt;ref&gt;G.W. Poulos &amp; Daniel Lindley. &quot;[http://www.wisegeek.com/what-is-a-flight-envelope.htm What Is a Flight Envelope?]&quot; ''WiseGeek'', 6 May 2014. Accessed: 16 May 2014.&lt;/ref&gt;

    <title>Pauline Flanagan</title>
    <ns>0</ns>

      <comment>Remove {{IBDB name}} parameter(s) migrated to Wikidata per [[Special:Permalink/742576273#Requests|request]]) ([[Project:AWB|AWB]] (12095)</comment>
